The authors successfully sequenced the variable regions of five mouse monoclonal IgG antibodies using this method, which enabled them to design chimeric mouse/human antibody expression plasmids, and all five recombinant antibodies bound their respective antigens with high affinity, confirming the sequences were correct.\n\n### Summary\n\nThe search did not reveal publicly available **variable region amino acid or nucleotide sequences** for anti-p21 ras mouse monoclonal antibodies. PMC\",\"url\":\"https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC367608/\"},{\"title\":\"Addgene: Browse Addgene's Antibodies\",\"url\":\"https://www.addgene.org/antibodies/all/\"},{\"title\":\"Addgene: Antibodies\",\"url\":\"https://www.addgene.org/antibodies/\"},{\"title\":\"Addgene: Antibody Plasmid Collection\",\"url\":\"https://www.addgene.org/collections/antibody-plasmids/\"},{\"title\":\"Addgene Begins Distribution of Recombinant Antibodies\",\"url\":\"https://blog.addgene.org/addgene-recombinant-antibodies-launch\"}]\n\nBased on my extensive search, here is a comprehensive summary of what is publicly available about the Y13-259 anti-Ras antibody and its sequences:\n\n## Y13-259 Anti-Ras Antibody — Summary of Available Information\n\n### Overview\nY13-259 is a recombinant monoclonal antibody to p21 protein, manufactured with variable regions (i.e., specificity) from the hybridoma Y13-259. It is a Rat IgG1, kappa monoclonal antibody.\n\n### Antigen / Epitope\nThe antibody binds to an epitope common to all p21ras isoforms (Glu63–Arg73), a region known as loop 4. More specifically, this antibody neutralizes the activity of H, K, and NRas by binding to residues Glu-63, Ser-65, Ala-66, Met-67, Gln-70, and Arg-73. Earlier epitope mapping studies found that by analysis of bacterially expressed p21 deletion mutants, the monoclonal antibody was found to interact with a region between positions 70 and 89 in the p21 amino acid sequence, and a highly conserved amino acid region between positions 70 and 81 was found to be the most likely site for the epitope.\n\n### Immunogen and Generation\nThe original antibody was generated by immunizing rats with Ha-MuSV-transformed NRK cells. Screening of sera identified animals with the strongest immune response against p21. Spleens were removed and cell fusion of immune lymphocytes with rat myeloma cell line 210RCY3 Ag 1.2.3 (Y3) was carried out. Supernatants were assayed for antibodies to p21 by GDP binding assay or immunofluorescence.\n\nThe antibody was first published in: Furth et al. \"Monoclonal antibodies to the p21 products of the transforming gene of Harvey murine sarcoma virus and of the cellular ras gene family.\" J Virol. 1982 Jul;43(1):294-304. PMID:6287003.\n\n### Cloning of Variable Region Genes\nThe immunoglobulin genes encoding the variable regions of the rat anti-p21ras antibody Y13-259 were molecularly cloned. These genes were reassembled into expression vectors supplying DNA sequences encoding human gamma 1 and kappa constant domains, yielding Hu-Y13-259, a secretory anti-p21ras antibody containing human constant regions. The antigen specificity of this recombinant antibody was demonstrated to be identical to that of the parental Y13-259, i.e., the amino acid sequence 60-76 of the p21ras protein.\n\n### CDR Sequences (Heavy Chain and Light Chain)\n**The actual CDR amino acid sequences of the Y13-259 heavy chain and light chain variable regions were not found in the publicly available search results.** The specific CDR sequences do not appear to be freely published in the indexed literature or standard antibody databases that were accessible through this search.\n\nHowever, there are two potential sources for obtaining the sequences:\n\n1. **Addgene (Antibody #198004):** Addgene lists amino acid sequences for this antibody but requires acceptance of their Affinity Reagent Sequence Policy to view them. This is likely the most accessible source for the sequences.\n\n2. **Absolute Antibody (Ab03219):** Absolute Antibody offers a recombinant monoclonal antibody to p21 protein, manufactured using their Recombinant Platform with variable regions from the hybridoma Y13-259.\n\n3. **Original cloning publication:** The variable region cloning was reported by Werge et al. (1990, FEBS Lett., PMID: 2123805) — \"Intracellular immunization. Cloning and intracellular expression of a monoclonal antibody to the p21ras protein.\"\n\n### Related Structural Information\n\nNote that the PDB structures 2UZI and 2VH5 contain crystal structures of HRAS complexed with an anti-RAS Fv, but these describe a single immunoglobulin variable region domain that specifically binds to activated GTP-bound RAS, where the variable region competitively binds to the conformationally variant regions of RAS where signalling effector molecules interact — this is a different anti-RAS antibody (a single-domain VH intrabody) from the Rabbitts lab, not Y13-259.\n\n### scFv Usage\nThe anti-p21ras Y13-259 single-chain Fv fragment (scFv) neutralizes the activity of p21-ras when intracellularly expressed in different systems. An engineered ultra-stable version called STAND-Y13-259 was developed. Previously, a neutralising rat monoclonal antibody, Y13-259 whole IgG, was developed against Ras small GTPases (Kras, Hras, and Nras), which have an oncogenic function.\n\n---\n\n**In summary:** To obtain the actual heavy and light chain CDR sequences of Y13-259, I would recommend checking the **Addgene page for antibody #198004** (which hosts the sequences behind their sequence access policy), the original cloning paper by **Werge et al. Multiple searches with different combinations of these sequences returned no direct matches.\n\n### What we know about antibody CDRs in general:\n\n- Complementarity-determining regions (CDRs) are polypeptide segments of the variable chains in immunoglobulins (antibodies). CDRs are where these molecules bind to their specific antigen and their structure/sequence determines the binding activity of the respective antibody.\n\n- There are three CDRs (CDR1, CDR2 and CDR3), arranged non-consecutively, on the amino acid sequence of a variable domain of an antigen receptor. Three can be found on the Light-chain (L1–L3) and three on the Heavy-chain (H1–H3). Since the antigen receptors are typically composed of two variable domains, there are six CDRs for each antigen receptor.\n\n### Possible approaches to identify the antibody:\n\nBased on the sequence characteristics:\n- **GYSFTTYTIH** (10 residues) — likely a **CDR-H1** sequence (Kabat definition), rich in tyrosine and threonine, which is typical\n- **EKFYGYDYW** (9 residues) — could be a **CDR-H3** sequence, with aromatic residues (F, Y, W) that are common in heavy chain CDR3\n- **FQGSHVPYT** (9 residues) — could be a **CDR-L3** sequence\n\nCDRH3 shows high length diversity and amino acid variability, with increased aromatic residue usage, particularly tyrosine.\n\n### Recommended next steps:\n\nTo identify which antibody these CDR sequences belong to and its target protein, I would recommend:\n\n1. **Searching the SAbDab (Structural Antibody Database)** — You can go to the Search CDRs page, choose which CDR definition to use (Chothia, Kabat, Contact, IMGT, or North), and choose the type of CDR you wish to select (H1, H2, H3, L1, L2 or L3).\n\n2. **Using the IMGT database** at http://www.imgt.org, which \"contains a large database of immunoglobulin and TCR sequences, as well as a multiplicity of software tools for their analysis.\"\n\n3. **BLAST searching** the sequences against antibody sequence databases such as those in NCBI or IMGT to find matching antibody entries.\n\nThese CDR sequences may belong to a proprietary/patented antibody, an experimental antibody from a specific research publication, or an entry in a specialized database that is not broadly indexed by web search engines.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"parent_tool_use_id":"toolu_01VHmWMq8E3z3rnRPNikdZuR","session_id":"11f2e5b3-afa2-4c57-ab5d-6ce97a94a375","uuid":"855fc2ea-46e3-490c-b237-4e3ab486d631"}

It was released on 2007-06-26 and deposited by Tanaka, T., Williams, R.L., and Rabbitts, T.H. The structure was determined at the MRC Laboratory of Molecular Biology in Cambridge, UK.\n\n### Biological Significance\nMany disease-related processes occur via protein complexes that are considered undruggable with small molecules. An example is RAS, which is frequently mutated in cancer and contributes to initiation and maintenance of the disease by constitutive signal transduction through protein interaction with effector proteins, like PI3K, RAF and RALGDS. Such protein interactions are therefore significant targets for therapy. The authors describe a single immunoglobulin variable region domain that specifically binds to activated GTP-bound RAS and prevents RAS-dependent tumorigenesis in a mouse model.\n\nThe crystal structure of the immunoglobulin-RAS complex shows that the variable region competitively binds to the conformationally variant regions of RAS, where its signalling effector molecules interact. This allows the plasma membrane targeted single domain intrabody to inhibit signalling by mutant RAS.\n\n### Structure Composition\nThe structure has asymmetric (C1) global symmetry and is a hetero 3-mer (A1B1C1). It contains three chains:\n- **Chain A**: HRAS (G12V mutant)\n- **Chain H**: Anti-RAS Fv heavy chain\n- **Chain L**: Anti-RAS Fv light chain\n\n### Light Chain Variable Region Sequence\nThe light chain (Chain L) is 104 amino acids long with a theoretical weight of 11.22 KDa. The source organism is Homo sapiens and the expression system is Escherichia coli BL21(DE3).\n\nThe light chain sequence from PDBe begins with: `>pdb|2uzi|L IQMTQSPSSLSASVGDRVTITCRASQSISSYLNWYQQKPGEAPKLLIYSASVLQSGVPSRFSGSGSGTDFTLTISSLQPEDFATYYCQQSVMIPMTFGQGTKVE...`\n\n### Heavy Chain Variable Region\nThe heavy chain sequence for chain H was not fully returned in the search results, but the PDBe entry for the heavy chain (protein entity 1) would be available at `https://www.ebi.ac.uk/pdbe/entry/pdb/2uzi/protein/1`.\n\n### Connection to Y13-259 Antibody\nMontano X and Jimenez A demonstrated that intracellular expression of the monoclonal anti-ras antibody Y13-259 blocks the transforming activity of ras oncogenes (Cell Growth Differ, 1995). The anti-RAS Fv in PDB 2UZI is derived from this lineage of anti-RAS antibodies, engineered as an intracellular antibody (intrabody) fragment. The scFv in PDB 2UZI is noted among scaffolds described for targeting Ras.\n\n### Related Structure\nA related structure, PDB 2VH5, contains the crystal structure of HRAS(G12V) in complex with a disulfide-free mutant of the anti-RAS Fv, revealing that there is no structural or functional difference with or without the intra-domain disulfide bond of the variable domain of heavy chain or the variable domain of light chain.\n\n### How to Access Full Sequences\nTo obtain the complete heavy chain and light chain variable region sequences for PDB 2UZI, you can visit:\n- **RCSB PDB**: https://www.rcsb.org/structure/2UZI (go to \"Sequence\" tab)\n- **PDBe Light Chain**: https://www.ebi.ac.uk/pdbe/entry/pdb/2uzi/protein/2\n- **PDBe Heavy Chain**: https://www.ebi.ac.uk/pdbe/entry/pdb/2uzi/protein/1\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"parent_tool_use_id":"toolu_01VHmWMq8E3z3rnRPNikdZuR","session_id":"11f2e5b3-afa2-4c57-ab5d-6ce97a94a375","uuid":"1a6267cb-9569-414a-8b77-cd50061eb405"}

Specifically:\n\n- The **DVLMTQ** motif at the N-terminus is a well-known framework 1 (FR1) signature of murine kappa light chains, commonly associated with the **Vκ** gene family.\n- The segment **RSSQSIVHRNGNTYLEWYL** contains what appears to be **CDR1** (complementarity-determining region 1) of the light chain, which is involved in antigen recognition.\n- The **LKPGQ** portion at the end corresponds to the beginning of framework 2 (FR2).\n\nThis type of sequence is frequently encountered in murine monoclonal antibodies and is often found in antibody engineering contexts such as humanization or construction of recombinant antibody fragments.\n\n## Relevant Background from Search Results\n\n- Light chains possess a variable domain (VL) and a constant domain (CL). The VL domain contains three hypervariable regions, also known as complementarity-determining regions (CDRs), which directly interact with antigens.\n\n- Each Fab fragment consists of one variable domain from a heavy chain (VH) and one variable domain from a light chain (VL), forming the antigen-binding site. The specificity of antibody-antigen interactions is primarily determined by the unique combination of VH and VL domains.\n\n- The antibody light chain (LC) consists of two domains and is essential for antigen binding in mature immunoglobulins. The two domains are connected by a highly conserved linker that comprises the structurally important Arg108 residue.\n\n- In most mammals, antibodies are composed of heavy and light chains that are generated sequentially by recombination of V, D (for heavy chains), J and C gene segments. Each chain contains three complementarity-determining regions (CDR1–CDR3), which contribute to antigen specificity. Certain heavy and light chains are preferred for particular antigens.\n\n- The specificity of Fab \"is not determined by the individual antibody chain but by the correct pairing of H and L chain.\"\n\nIf you need to identify the exact antibody or patent this sequence belongs to, I would recommend searching it in databases like **NCBI BLAST (IgBLAST)**, the **IMGT database**, or the **Kabat database**, which are specifically designed for antibody sequence annotation and identification.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"parent_tool_use_id":"toolu_01VHmWMq8E3z3rnRPNikdZuR","session_id":"11f2e5b3-afa2-4c57-ab5d-6ce97a94a375","uuid":"0d41804c-eb6a-47e7-aeea-25e957e6054a"}

Cloning and intracellular expression of a monoclonal antibody to the p21ras protein\"**\n\nBy T.M. Werge, S. Biocca, and A. Cattaneo, published in *FEBS Letters*, 1990 Nov 12; 274(1-2):193-198. DOI: 10.1016/0014-5793(90)81362-r.\n\n**PMID:** 2123805\n\n### Summary of the Paper\n\nFollowing the demonstration that intracellular expression of antibodies ('intracellular immunization') may be utilized to engineer new traits in mammalian cells, the authors undertook experiments to perturb the function of p21ras proteins by engineering the intracellular expression of the anti-p21ras antibody Y13-259.\n\nThe variable regions of this antibody were cloned and, after verifying their antigen binding activity, expressed in general purpose vectors for the intracellular expression of antibodies.\n\nThe results confirmed that the cloned antibody was efficiently expressed both in the secretory and the intracellular forms, demonstrating that intracellular immunization of mammalian cells against p21ras, or any other antigen for which a monoclonal antibody is available, can now be performed.\n\n### Impact and Follow-up Work\n\nThis paper was highly influential in the field of intracellular antibodies (intrabodies) and has been widely cited. Key follow-up studies include:\n\n1. The variable regions of Y13-259 were subsequently cloned into vectors for expression of either the whole antibody molecule or its single-chain Fv fragment (ScFv) derivative. The hydrophobic leader sequence for secretion was mutated or deleted to target the recombinant antibodies to the cytosol. When expressed in the cytosol of *Xenopus laevis* oocytes, the antibodies colocalized with endogenous p21ras protein and markedly inhibited H1 kinase activity induced by insulin, with cytosolic anti-p21ras ScFv fragments blocking meiotic maturation. (Biocca et al., 1994, *Nature Biotechnology*)\n\n2. A cytoplasmic single chain Fv version of the Y13-259 anti-Ras antibody was later constructed and co-transfected into the human lymphoid cell line Jurkat, where the Ras-specific antibody interfered with NF-AT activation upon direct activation of the T-cell antigen receptor. (Werge et al., 1994, *FEBS Letters*)\n\n3. Cardinale and co-workers later showed that when the scFv format of the Y13-259 antibody was expressed in a eukaryotic cell system, it was highly aggregating intracellularly, thereby trapping intracellular Ras in an insoluble complex that could be subsequently degraded by the cell.\n\nThe paper is available as a free article on PubMed at: https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/2123805/\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"parent_tool_use_id":"toolu_01VHmWMq8E3z3rnRPNikdZuR","session_id":"11f2e5b3-afa2-4c57-ab5d-6ce97a94a375","uuid":"d1f4713b-e5cc-47e3-b839-827405d71edf"}

PubMed\",\"url\":\"https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/7647040/\"}]\n\nBased on my search results, here is a comprehensive summary of findings related to the PDB crystal structure of the antibody Fab complex with p21 H-Ras and the Y13-259 antibody:\n\n## Key Findings\n\n### PDB Entry: 2UZI — Anti-RAS Antibody / H-Ras Complex\nPDB entry **2UZI** is the crystal structure of an **HRAS(G12V) – anti-RAS Fv complex**. While this is not specifically the Y13-259 Fab, it is a closely related anti-Ras antibody-RAS complex. The structure describes a single immunoglobulin variable region domain that specifically binds to activated GTP-bound RAS, and the crystal structure shows that the variable region competitively binds to the conformationally variant regions of RAS where its signalling effector molecules interact.\n\n### Y13-259 Antibody — Epitope Mapping on p21 Ras\n\nNo dedicated PDB crystal structure of the **Y13-259 Fab** in complex with H-Ras p21 was found in the search results. However, extensive epitope mapping studies exist:\n\n- The structural domain within the p21 molecule recognized by the Y13-259 monoclonal antibody was localized. By analysis of a series of bacterially expressed p21 deletion mutants, the monoclonal antibody was found to interact with a region between positions 70 and 89 in the p21 amino acid sequence. By comparison of the coding sequences of different p21 proteins, a highly conserved amino acid region between positions 70 and 81 was found to be the most likely site for the epitope.\n\n- More specifically, the antibody binds to an epitope common to all p21ras isoforms (Glu63–Arg73), a region known as loop 4.\n\n### Y13-259 Antibody Background\n\n- The Y13-259 antibody reacts to p21 encoded by Ha-MuSV v-ras gene and cross-reacts to p21 encoded by Kirsten MuSV v-ras gene, p21 encoded by BALB-SV, and 29kDa gag-ras fusion protein encoded by Ra-SV.\n\n- Microinjection of the anti-ras antibody Mab Y13-259 modifies ras function and can induce temporary reversion of the transformed phenotype in mutant ras-transformed cells.\n\n- The genes coding for the heavy and light chains of Mab Y13-259 were isolated from a cDNA library. NIH3T3 cells transfected with heavy and light chain expression vectors produced functional anti-ras antibody.\n\n### Related H-Ras p21 Crystal Structures in the PDB\n\nSeveral H-Ras p21 crystal structures are available, though not in complex with Y13-259:\n\n- **5P21**: Refined crystal structure of the triphosphate conformation of H-Ras p21 at 1.35 Å resolution.\n- **1JAI**: H-Ras p21 protein mutant G12P, complexed with GppCp and manganese.\n- **521P**: Three-dimensional structures of H-Ras p21 mutants — molecular basis for their inability to function as signal switch molecules.\n\n### Summary\n\nIt appears that a crystal structure of the **Y13-259 Fab** directly in complex with H-Ras p21 has **not been deposited in the PDB** (or was not found in the current search). The closest related structure is **PDB 2UZI**, which is an anti-Ras single-domain antibody (Fv) complex with HRAS(G12V). The Y13-259 epitope has been characterized biochemically to reside in the region around **residues 63–89** of p21 Ras (loop 4), but this was determined through deletion mutagenesis and peptide competition studies rather than X-ray crystallography of the antibody-antigen complex.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"parent_tool_use_id":"toolu_01VHmWMq8E3z3rnRPNikdZuR","session_id":"11f2e5b3-afa2-4c57-ab5d-6ce97a94a375","uuid":"1df88eee-1783-4492-a01c-5306e744353d"}

Specifically:\n\n- The **\"QVQL\"** motif at the N-terminus is a hallmark of a **VH domain** framework region 1 (FR1), commonly found in murine or humanized antibodies.\n- This particular sequence pattern is associated with certain **VH gene family** germline segments.\n\n## General Background on Antibody Heavy Chains\n\n- Human immunoglobulins are Y-shaped proteins composed of two identical light chains (LCs) and two identical heavy chains (HCs).\n\n- The amino acid sequences of many immunoglobulin heavy and light chains have been determined and reveal two important features of antibody molecules. First, each chain consists of a series of similar, although not identical, sequences, each about 110 amino acids long. Each of these repeats corresponds to a discrete, compactly folded region of protein structure known as a protein domain.\n\n- The second important feature revealed by comparisons of amino acid sequences is that the amino-terminal sequences of both the heavy and light chains vary greatly between different antibodies. The variability in sequence is limited to approximately the first 110 amino acids, corresponding to the first domain.\n\n- The complete nucleotide sequence of the 957-kb DNA of the human immunoglobulin heavy chain variable (VH) region locus was determined and 43 novel VH segments were identified. The region contains 123 VH segments classifiable into seven different families, of which 79 are pseudogenes. Of the 44 VH segments with an open reading frame, 39 are expressed as heavy chain proteins and 1 as mRNA.\n\n- The V regions are encoded by two or three genetic segments, namely V, D, and J segments, each of which comprises multiple copies and provides the repertoire before somatic mutation. During the ontogeny of lymphocytes, each one of these segments is chosen to undergo a somatic recombination event called V-(D)-J recombination, giving rise to the combinatorial and junctional amino acid diversity.\n\n## How to Find This Specific Sequence in NCBI\n\nTo locate the specific protein entry for **QVQLQQSAAELARPGAS** in the NCBI database, I would recommend:\n\n1. **NCBI Protein BLAST**: Go to [https://blast.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/](https://blast.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/) and run a **BLASTp** search with the sequence `QVQLQQSAAELARPGAS`. Monoclonal Anti-vH RAS reacts with phosphorylated and non-phosphorylated forms of vH RAS and vK RAS p21's and reacts with the p21 transitional products of the H, K, and N ras human genes. This antibody neutralizes the activity of H, K, and NRas by binding to residues Glu-63, Ser-65, Ala-66, Met-67, Gln-70 and Arg-73.\n\n### Epitope\nBy analysis of a series of bacterially expressed p21 deletion mutants, the monoclonal antibody was found to interact with a region between positions 70 and 89 in the p21 amino acid sequence. By comparison of the coding sequences of different p21 proteins recognized by this monoclonal antibody, a highly conserved amino acid region between positions 70 and 81 was found to be the most likely site for the epitope detected by the Y13-259 antibody.\n\n### Sequence Information\nThe genes coding for the heavy and light chains of Mab Y13-259 were isolated from a cDNA library. NIH3T3 cells transfected with heavy and light chain expression vectors produced functional anti-ras antibody.\n\nNotably, Cochet et al. reported intracellular expression and functional properties of an anti-p21Ras scFv derived from a rat hybridoma containing specific lambda and irrelevant kappa light chains. This indicates the functional light chain of Y13-259 is a **lambda** chain, which is important since the hybridoma also produces a non-functional kappa chain from the myeloma fusion partner.\n\n### Variable Region Sequence — Not Found with Specified Motifs\nThe specific amino acid sequence motifs searched for — **QVQLQQ**, **DVLMTQ**, **GYSFTTYTIH**, and **EKFYGYDYW** — were **not found** in the search results in direct association with Y13-259. Here is a summary of what the searches revealed:\n\n## Search Results Summary\n\n### About SAbDab (The Structural Antibody Database)\n\nSAbDab is a database containing all the antibody structures available in the PDB, annotated and presented in a consistent fashion. It is a database devoted to automatically collecting, curating and presenting antibody structural data in a consistent manner for both bulk analysis and individual inspection.\n\nKey features of SAbDab include:\n- SAbDab updates on a weekly basis and provides users with a range of methods to select sets of structures — for example, users can select by species, experimental details (e.g. method, resolution and r-factor), similarity to a given antibody sequence, amino-acid composition at certain positions and antibody–antigen affinity.\n- Individual structures can be accessed via a structure viewer interface which shows a summary of the structure annotation, an interactive 3D representation of the structure, links to other databases alongside information for each antibody in the structure, including the chain identifiers, CDR sequences and full Fab sequence.\n\n### Chymotrypsin Structures Found (but not antibody-chymotrypsin complexes)\n\nThe PDB search returned several chymotrypsin structures, but these were complexes with **inhibitors**, not antibodies:\n- PDB 1CBW contains the crystal structures of the inhibitor domain of Alzheimer's amyloid beta-protein precursor (APPI) complexed to bovine chymotrypsin and basic pancreatic trypsin inhibitor (BPTI) bound to chymotrypsin.\n- PDB 5J4Q contains alpha-chymotrypsin from bovine pancreas in complex with Bowman-Birk inhibitor from soybean.\n\n### No Specific Antibody–Chymotrypsin Complex Found\n\nThe search did not return a specific PDB entry for a **mouse monoclonal antibody in complex with chymotrypsin** cataloged in SAbDab. The FLAG-tag, consisting of the DYKDDDDK peptide sequence, was originally designed to be a short hydrophilic purification handle with an internal protease cleavage site (Enterokinase) for protein identification and purification.\n\n## Anti-FLAG M2 Antibody\n\nAnti-FLAG M2 is the most popular antibody against the FLAG-tag, due to its ease of use, versatility, and availability in pure form or as bead conjugate. M2 binds N-terminal, C-terminal and internal FLAG-tags and binding is calcium-independent. One of the monoclonal antibodies against this peptide, anti-FLAG M2, recognises a FLAG peptide sequence at the N terminus, Met-N terminus, C terminus, or internal site of a fusion protein and has been extremely useful for the detection, identification, and purification of recombinant proteins.\n\n## PDB Structure 7BG1 — Apo Structure of Anti-FLAG M2 Fab\n\nAntibody sequence information is crucial to understanding the structural basis for antigen binding and enables the use of antibodies as therapeutics and research tools. The researchers demonstrated a method for direct de novo sequencing of monoclonal IgG from the purified antibody products, using a panel of multiple complementary proteases to generate suitable peptides for de novo sequencing by LC-MS/MS. The method achieves full sequence coverage of the monoclonal antibody herceptin, with an accuracy of 99% in the variable regions. They applied the method to sequence the widely used anti-FLAG-M2 mouse monoclonal antibody, which was successfully validated by remodeling a high-resolution crystal structure. This work is from Utrecht University.\n\n## PDB Structure 8RMO — Crystal Structure of Anti-FLAG M2 Fab Bound to FLAG Peptide\n\nThe researchers present an atomic resolution (1.17 Å) structure of the FLAG peptide in complex with the Fab of anti-FLAG M2, revealing key binding determinants. Five of the eight FLAG peptide residues form direct interactions with paratope residues. The FLAG peptide adopts a 3₁₀ helix conformation in complex with the Fab.\n\n### Key Structural Insights (from the associated publication):\n\n- As anticipated for a highly charged and hydrophilic epitope, most of the interactions formed between the FLAG peptide and anti-FLAG M2 are either through hydrogen bonds, salt bridges or ionic interactions. Five out of the eight FLAG peptide residues (Asp1, Tyr2, Lys3, Asp4 and Asp6) appear to contribute directly to the interaction with M2. FLAG peptide residues Tyr2, Lys3 and Asp4 appear to form crucial interactions, predominantly involving M2 residues heavy chain Glu99 and light chain Arg32.\n\n- Several ordered water molecules as well as two chloride ions were observed neighbouring the FLAG peptide binding site. Three of these water molecules simultaneously form hydrogen bonds with both paratope and FLAG peptide, mediating indirect interactions between residues FLAG Asp1 and light chain Tyr101, FLAG Tyr2 and heavy chain Tyr50, and between FLAG Asp6 and light chain Asn35.\n\n- An overlay of the apo (grey) anti-FLAG M2 structure (PDB 7BG1) and the complexed structure with FLAG peptide reveals structural differences.\n\n### Rational Mutations and Shorter FLAG-tag:\n\nThese structural insights allowed the researchers to rationally introduce point mutations on both the peptide and antibody side. They tested these by surface plasmon resonance, leading them to propose a shorter yet equally binding version of the FLAG-tag for the M2 antibody.\n\n## Earlier Work on Binding Specificity\n\nA previous study using a phage display combinatorial peptide library determined that the motif DYKxxD encompasses the critical amino acid residues responsible for the binding of FLAG peptide to this antibody.\n\n## Key References\n\n- **PDB 7BG1**: Apo anti-FLAG M2 Fab structure ([RCSB link](https://www.rcsb.org/structure/7BG1))\n- **PDB 8RMO**: Anti-FLAG M2 Fab in complex with FLAG peptide ([RCSB link](https://www.rcsb.org/structure/8RMO))\n- **Publication**: The coordinates and structure factors of the crystal structure of the FLAG/anti-FLAG M2 complex have been deposited at the protein databank under accession code 8RMO. The paper is titled \"Structural Basis for Recognition of the FLAG-tag by Anti-FLAG M2\" and is available on [ScienceDirect](https://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/pii/S0022283624002444) and [bioRxiv](https://www.biorxiv.org/content/10.1101/2024.03.25.586599v2.full).\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"parent_tool_use_id":"toolu_01VHmWMq8E3z3rnRPNikdZuR","session_id":"11f2e5b3-afa2-4c57-ab5d-6ce97a94a375","uuid":"a3abd31e-99b4-4a06-b681-428108e1833c"}
